- 2026-05-16 — **audit(agents): silent-arg-ignore in `alm-tools.ts` — `runRateShock` fixed as beachhead, 23 `as any` casts flagged for sweep.** Post-wave audit on recently-modified backend files turned up two distinct findings: **(1) clean result on error-handling**: scanned every catch block landed in the past 36h across `ai-advisor/`, `auth/`, `cpa/`, `close/guards/`, `realtime-alm/`, `agent-api/`, and the IDOR-guard adds. All 8 catch blocks either log + emit explicit error to caller (`client.emit('error', { code, message })`) or fall through to a documented role/value with a `logger.warn` trail. **Zero silent-failure regressions** in the recent IDOR/security wave — quality bar held. **(2) Silent-arg-ignore pattern in `backend-node/src/agents/registry/tools/alm-tools.ts`**: file has **24 `as any` casts** of the shape `(this.<service> as any).<method>(input.someArg)`. Sample inspection confirmed at least 3 of these silently ignore caller arguments: **`runRateShock`** (passed `shockBps` array as 2nd arg to a single-arg `YieldCurveService.getYieldCurveAnalysis` → ignored at runtime, agent's "Rate shock computed for N scenarios" summary lied about scenario-specific computation); **`getPeerAnalytics`** (passes `input.metric` as 2nd arg to single-arg `PeerAnalyticsService.getPeerAnalytics` → metric ignored); **`runSimulation`** (passes `input.paths` as a *number* where the service signature expects an *opts object* `{ paths?, quarters?, ... }` → JS evaluates `(numericValue)?.paths` as `undefined`, default 10000 paths is used regardless of caller input). The `as any` casts mask TypeScript's arity/shape checks; JS silently drops/ignores the extra arg; the agent's user-facing summary CLAIMS scenario-specific output but returns the unconditional service default. **This violates the "Never silent zeros" quality bar** even more concerning than silent-zeros because the user gets *wrong-but-plausible* numbers. **This commit ships a beachhead fix** for `runRateShock` only — drops the `as any` cast (so TS now type-checks the call), removes the dead 2nd argument, and updates the summary to be honest: `"Rate shock analysis returned. N caller-specified scenario(s) requested; analysis covers the standard Basel shock set (custom shock values not yet supported by YieldCurveService)."` 17-line inline comment explains the long-standing bug and the path to a proper fix (add `shocks?: number[]` to `YieldCurveService.getYieldCurveAnalysis`). Behavior preserved (the data returned was already the same — service was always running the Basel set); the lie was in the summary text. **Known-affected tools flagged for next-session sweep** (rest of the 24 `as any` sites: `getYieldCurveAnalysis` × 1 (this commit), `getAdvancedLiquidity`, `getCECLAnalysis`, `getConcentrationAnalysis`, `getIRRPolicy`, `getPeerAnalytics` × 2, `getRepricingGap`, `runSimulation` × 1, `getEarlyWarning`, `computeHealthScore`, `getFTPAnalysis`, `getDepositBeta`, `capitalAdequacy` chain, `complianceCalendar` chain, `getExamPrep`, `runFullStressTest`, `runCustomScenario`, `analyzeDecay`, `priceDeposit`). For each: spot-check the service's actual signature vs the call site, remove `as any` where the call is correct, fix the call where args mismatch. **Why not do all 24 here:** each requires reading the corresponding service to know whether the call is right or the service is missing a parameter. Doing them in one commit risks introducing real behavior changes without per-tool review. The beachhead establishes the pattern and proves the fix is safe; the sweep is the next-session continuation. **Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean across `backend-node` after dropping the cast (proves the typed call signature works); `npx jest --testPathPatterns="agents"` → 9 suites / 89 tests green; `npx eslint --quiet` on the touched file clean. Behavior diff: data field is unchanged (service was always returning the Basel set); summary now correctly reflects that custom shocks aren't honored. — `backend-node/src/agents/registry/tools/alm-tools.ts`

- 2026-05-16 — **security(agent-api): close body-override IDOR in `AgentRunsController.triggerRun` — URL `:institutionId` wins over body.** Body-trust audit follow-up to the IDOR sweep. Pre-fix: `agent-runs.controller.ts:87` had `institutionId: req.institutionId ?? institutionId` where `req` is the parsed body. The class-level `@UseGuards(AuthGuard, InstitutionScopeGuard)` verified ownership of the URL `:institutionId`, but a caller authorized for institution-A could then post `body.institutionId = 'attacker-target'` and the `?? institutionId` fallback would silently override the URL value, calling `runner.run({ institutionId: 'attacker-target', ... })`. **The guard's verification was made meaningless by the controller's argument-merging order** — exactly the kind of subtle post-guard subversion the verifier can't catch (it scans `@UseGuards` presence, not actual data-flow). **Fix:** drop the body fallback entirely — `institutionId,` from the URL is the only source. Body's `institutionId` field stays in `RunAgentRequestSchema` as `.optional()` for backward-compat with clients that send it; the value is silently ignored. The idempotency-key hash already used URL `:institutionId` (line 96) so no collision-attack risk via body either. 8-line comment block explains the contract above the runner.run call. **Spec lock:** new test in `agent-runs.controller.spec.ts` — `triggerRun(INST_ID, { ..., institutionId: 'attacker-target-inst' })` MUST result in `runner.run` called with `institutionId: INST_ID`. Plus a `not.objectContaining({ institutionId: 'attacker-target-inst' })` assertion as defense-in-depth so a future refactor that re-introduces the body-override fails this test loudly. Spec count 11 → **12 green**. **Audit findings (parallel body-trust sweep — not all fixed in this commit, scope discipline):** (a) **`agent-eval/agent-eval.controller.ts`** has `@Controller('api/v1/eval')` with **NO `@UseGuards` at all** — both `POST /golden` and `POST /replay` accept `body.institutionId` and pass straight to services. Comment at L43 says "Protected by admin guard in production" but no guard exists in source. **CRITICAL follow-up.** Out of this commit's scope to keep the body-override fix reviewable in isolation; will be a separate tight commit. (b) **`realtime-alm/market-data.controller.ts`** has 5 DTOs with `institutionId` in body. Per `b86baed8`, the controller has method-level `@UseGuards(AuthTenantGuard, InstitutionScopeGuard)` on the 3 alert routes. Need to verify those guards actually catch the body-supplied value (vs URL). Quick spot-check follow-up. (c) **`cpa/cpa.dto.ts:72` `AddClientSchema`** — used by `POST /api/cpa/firms/:firmId/clients` to add an institution to a firm's client list. By design, the body's institutionId is the *target* of the new relationship; no prior relationship to verify. Whether "any firm member can claim any institution as a client" is a feature or a bug depends on the CPA onboarding workflow (out-of-band consent vs. self-service). Documented as design question, not a fix. **Internal-vs-external sweep:** `backend-node/src/agents/contracts/*.ts` define institutionId in body schemas for internal agent IO — these are NOT HTTP request bodies, they're agent runner contracts. Skipped (not attack surfaces). **Verification:** `tsc --noEmit` clean across `backend-node`; **12/12 green** on `agent-runs.controller.spec.ts` (was 11, +1 IDOR lock); `npm run verify:institution-scope` unchanged at `156/156, 0 violations`. Atomic stage+commit via `git commit -- <pathspec>` per protocol. — `backend-node/src/agent-api/agent-runs.controller.ts`, `backend-node/src/agent-api/__tests__/agent-runs.controller.spec.ts`

- 2026-05-16 — **fix(cpa): rename `firmId`/`brandingOverride`/`addedAt` → schema-canonical `cpaFirmId`/`reportBrandingOverride`/`assignedAt` in Prisma queries across cpa-client/cpa-branding/cpa-firm services.** **Real production bug, surfaced while building `FirmOwnsClientGuard` in `0cf2c87c`.** Schema at `prisma/schema.prisma:2523-2527` defines the `CpaClientRelationship` fields as `cpaFirmId @map("cpa_firm_id")`, `assignedAt @map("assigned_at")`, `reportBrandingOverride @map("report_branding_override")` — but the three CPA services were querying with the non-canonical names `firmId`, `addedAt`, `brandingOverride`. **Prisma 4+ throws `PrismaClientValidationError` on unknown arguments**, so every `addClient`, `removeClient`, `listClients`, `getReportBranding`, and `getFirm` call would have crashed at runtime when the CPA white-label feature was exercised against the real database. Tests passed only because they mock `prisma.cpaClientRelationship.findFirst`/`findMany`/`create`/`update` and never see the validation error. **6 query sites fixed** across 3 service files: `cpa-client.service.ts` (5 — 4 `where` clauses on `cpaClientRelationship.findFirst`/`findMany`, 1 `create.data`, 1 `update.data` reactivation path, 1 `orderBy` on `listClients`), `cpa-branding.service.ts` (1 `where` clause + 3 JS property reads on returned relationship: `relationship.brandingOverride` would have been undefined post-fix and incorrectly returned base branding without overrides — independent bug class on the same model), `cpa-firm.service.ts` (1 `orderBy` inside an `include: { clients: { ... } }` clause on `getFirm`). **Verifier scan continues to report 0 violations** — bug was at the Prisma-arg level, not at the controller-guard level, so the verifier never flagged it (different layer). **Spec update:** `cpa-client.service.spec.ts:79-87` `toHaveBeenCalledWith` assertion updated from `data: containing { firmId: 'firm-1', ... }` to `data: containing { cpaFirmId: 'firm-1', ... }` — explicit lock against regression. Other test fixtures (mock-return values with `firmId`/`brandingOverride`/`addedAt`) left as-is since the service no longer reads them post-fix; cleanup of dead mock-fixture fields is a separate hygiene concern. **API surface preserved:** DTO field name `brandingOverride` (input parameter on `addClient`) stays — only the Prisma-boundary translation changes. Existing API consumers see no contract change. **Verification:** `tsc --noEmit` clean across `backend-node`; **45/45 green** across all 3 cpa specs; `npm run verify:institution-scope` unchanged at `156/156, 0 violations`. Atomic stage+commit via `git commit -- <pathspec>` per inter-session protocol. — `backend-node/src/cpa/cpa-client.service.ts`, `backend-node/src/cpa/cpa-branding.service.ts`, `backend-node/src/cpa/cpa-firm.service.ts`, `backend-node/src/cpa/cpa-client.service.spec.ts`

- 2026-05-16 — **Audit doc: `docs/security/AUTH_COVERAGE_AUDIT.md` — sweep of 24 unguarded-at-class-level controllers, 3 CRITICAL real gaps identified, 5 auth patterns catalogued.** Companion to the IDOR sweep, opening the next-tier security invariant: "every route's authentication story is explicit and enforced." Methodology mirrors `IDOR_RESIDUAL_AUDIT.md` (per-controller matrix, status legend, fix recipes, sweep coordination notes). **Five auth patterns identified in CerniQ:** (1) canonical class-level `@UseGuards(Auth*)` — what the multi-rule verifier locks; (2) method-level `@UseGuards` per route — for mixed public/scoped controllers; (3) inline `verifyAdmin(adminKey)` + `x-admin-key` constant-time compare — admin endpoints; (4) inline `validateApiKey()` + `x-api-key` lookup — external API surface; (5) public by design — health/auth/marketing/webhooks. **3 CRITICAL real gaps documented:** `agents/agents.controller.ts` (3 routes — `POST /agents/run` accepts `institutionId` + `organizationId` from body with zero auth, the agent-runner can be triggered by anyone with knowledge of the URL on any tenant), `agent-trust/agent-trust.controller.ts` (1 route — `POST /api/v1/trust/validate` claims "Protected by AuthGuard in production (added at AppModule level)" but the only `APP_GUARD` is `UserThrottleGuard`; docstring is aspirational not factual), `agent-eval/agent-eval.controller.ts` (2 routes — `POST /eval/golden` + `POST /eval/replay`, same aspirational-docstring problem). All three look like legacy precursors to `agent-api/agent-runs.controller.ts` (the modern equivalent at `@Controller('api/v1/agents/:institutionId')` with `@UseGuards(AuthGuard, InstitutionScopeGuard)`). Fix sketches mirror peer-2's ai-advisor body-IDOR pattern (`e88ae20c`/`4f9e2728`) — inject the guard, call `verifyOwnership(institutionId, userId, isMasterCeo)` in each handler before service work. The `organizationId`-from-body case in `agents.controller.ts` is currently blocked on a missing primitive: `OrgMembershipGuard.verifyMembership(orgId, userId)` doesn't exist yet (mirror peer-2's `verifyOwnership` extraction from `InstitutionScopeGuard.canActivate` in `b2a64c25`). **Cursor IDOR sub-audit closed with NO gaps:** the `IDOR_RESIDUAL_AUDIT.md` flagged follow-up "audit the rest of the keyset-paginated endpoints" is closed — only 2 controllers use cursor pagination in CerniQ (`agent-api/agent-runs.controller.ts`, `agent-api/alerts.controller.ts`), both already validate that cursor row's `institutionId` matches the requester's. `cossec/cossec.dto.ts:61` has a dead-code `cursor` field (no consumer; cleanup opportunity). All other paginated endpoints use offset/limit with tenant key in URL path, gated by the canonical guards — cursor-IDOR class is unreachable there. **Recommended primitive-consolidation work** flagged for future waves: extract `AdminKeyGuard` from the inline `verifyAdmin()` helper duplicated across 6 controllers; extract `OrgMembershipGuard.verifyMembership()` to unblock the agents-controller fix; build `verify-auth-coverage.mjs` parallel to the tenant-scope verifier. The 25 intentional-public routes in the matrix all get `// verify:auth-skip — <pattern>` annotations when that script lands. **Coordination:** the audit doc is a NEW file co-existing with peer-2-claimed `IDOR_RESIDUAL_AUDIT.md` so the claim doesn't block. The 3 critical gaps + 3 primitive-consolidation items are open scope for any peer to pick up — each independent. **Verification methodology:** the audit doc itself is the deliverable — no code change in this commit. Findings reproducible via the awk-based per-controller classification recorded in the doc's TL;DR. — `docs/security/AUTH_COVERAGE_AUDIT.md` (NEW)

- 2026-05-16 — **ci(verifier): add 4th rule `firm-owns-client` to `verify-institution-scope-guard.mjs` — locks `FirmOwnsClientGuard` requirement on `(:firmId + :institutionId)` routes.** Companion CI lock for `0cf2c87c`'s `FirmOwnsClientGuard`: mirrors peer's earlier `OrgMembershipGuard` extension (`137ee765`) that added `org-membership` + `close-cycle-membership` as rules 2 + 3. With this commit, the verifier covers all 4 of the wave's tenancy primitives. **Schema extension:** new optional `secondaryParam` field on RULES entries. When set, the rule fires ONLY when the effective path contains BOTH `:canonicalParam` AND `:secondaryParam`. Two-line conditional in the R2 check + parallel conditional in the perRuleTotals walk. Backward-compatible — existing 3 rules don't set `secondaryParam` and behave identically. **New rule:** `firm-owns-client` with `canonicalParam: 'institutionId'`, `secondaryParam: 'firmId'`, `guard: 'FirmOwnsClientGuard'`, model `CpaClientRelationship (cpaFirmId, institutionId, removedAt: null)`. References commit `0cf2c87c` in docRef. **Self-test:** 3 new fixture cases — (a) `:firmId/clients/:institutionId` with `FirmOwnsClientGuard` at class level → 0 errors (OK), (b) same shape without `FirmOwnsClientGuard` and no skip comment → 2 errors (both `institution-scope/R2` and `firm-owns-client/R2` fire independently — locked invariant proves the rule actually catches absent guards), (c) `:firmId` alone with no `:institutionId` → 0 errors (rule correctly does NOT fire on single-param routes — proves the `secondaryParam` filter works). Self-test count grew from 18 to **21 cases passing**. **Production scan post-extension:** `60 controller(s) scanned [institution-scope: 132/132, org-membership: 12/12, close-cycle-membership: 11/11, firm-owns-client: 1/1], 0 violation(s)`. Total = **156 routes provably guarded across 4 ownership patterns**, up from 155 (the CPA `DELETE clients/:institutionId` is the 1 firm-owns-client route). The CPA route's existing `verify:tenant-scope-skip` comment continues to exempt it from `institution-scope` (legitimate — `InstitutionScopeGuard.Workspace.ownerId` model doesn't fit CPA firms), AND `FirmOwnsClientGuard` is present at class level so `firm-owns-client/R2` passes via the guarded path (not via the skip). **Known limitation documented inline:** skip comments are rule-agnostic — exempt all matching rules. If someone removed `FirmOwnsClientGuard` from `CpaClientController` the skip comment would also exempt the new `firm-owns-client` rule, silently regressing the lock. The spec for `FirmOwnsClientGuard` (9 unit tests from `0cf2c87c`) catches removal via failing tests; a future verifier improvement would add rule-targeted skip syntax (`// verify:tenant-scope-skip[rule-id] — ...`) for explicit per-rule exemption. **Out of scope for this tightly-scoped commit.** **Verification:** verifier `--self-test` → `21 case(s) pass` (was 18, +3); production scan → `156/156 guarded, 0 violations`. Single-file edit (`backend-node/scripts/verify-institution-scope-guard.mjs`) — no `tsc` or `jest` needed since the script is plain Node ESM with no TS types and the self-test IS the test. Prettier clean. `claude-peers conflict-check` OK. Atomic stage+commit via `git commit -- <pathspec>` per inter-session protocol. — `backend-node/scripts/verify-institution-scope-guard.mjs`

- 2026-05-16 — **Audit-doc multi-param-rule limitation note + retro-attribution for tsc-hard-block bundled in `a5fc6637`.** Two doc changes. **(1) `docs/security/IDOR_RESIDUAL_AUDIT.md` §"CI enforcement — CLOSED" correction:** my prior commit `a5fc6637` claimed the planned `FirmOwnsClientGuard` would slot in as "a one-line `RULES` table entry + one self-test fixture, no parser changes." That claim was wrong once I read peer `sid=8f694e66`'s shipped `FirmOwnsClientGuard` (commit body in handoff entry below): the new guard is a *conjunction* case (only applies when a route has BOTH `:firmId` AND `:institutionId`), and `CpaFirmController` has 5 `:firmId`-only routes that legitimately don't need it. The current single-canonical-param `RULES` schema can't express that without a parser-level extension (e.g. a `pathRequires: string[]` field that ANDs multiple param tokens before R2 fires). Replaced the over-optimistic claim with an explicit "Known framework limitation — multi-param rules" note that documents (a) why the CPA route is already protected (class-level `@UseGuards(AuthGuard, RolesGuard, FirmOwnsClientGuard)` + existing `// verify:institution-scope-skip` comment + 9 unit tests in the guard spec), and (b) the future-enhancement path if a second conjunction case appears. Peer notified via inbox `a3a8b8ae`; this handoff entry is the option-1 retro-attribution. **Coordination postmortem:** inverse of the `feedback_shared_tree_git_coordination.md` `git add -A` footgun — peer's *pre-staged* work in a shared index swept by my bare `git commit`. Defense (and the protocol cardinal rule from `feedback_inter_session_protocol.md`): always use `git commit -- <pathspec>` to scope commits to explicitly-named files, never bare `git commit` on a shared-tree index. Used correctly in `137ee765` (manual `git reset HEAD` + explicit `git add` + bare commit on an empty-otherwise index); the defense slipped here because I'd only added one file and assumed the index was otherwise clean. **No code change in this commit** — both files touched are docs-only; landing-gate auto-allowed. — `docs/security/IDOR_RESIDUAL_AUDIT.md`, `docs/SESSION_HANDOFF.md`

- 2026-05-16 — **security(ai-advisor): Supabase JWT fallback in WS gateway — mirrors `AuthGuard.verifySupabaseToken` so multi-provider clients aren't locked out.** Closes the documented follow-up from `b2a64c25`'s audit entry: the WS gateway's `verifyClientToken` only handled legacy JWTs via `JwtService.verify`. Deployments where some clients authenticate with Supabase tokens (per `AuthGuard:374`'s production-grade two-stage logic) would be rejected at the WS handshake even though the same tokens work fine on the HTTP side. **Refactor:** `verifyClientToken` becomes a two-stage dispatcher: (1) `tryVerifyLegacyJwt` — synchronous, shared-secret, zero network, fastest path; (2) `tryVerifySupabaseToken` — only runs if both `SUPABASE_URL` and (`SUPABASE_ANON_KEY` || `NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY`) are present, HTTPs to `${SUPABASE_URL}/auth/v1/user` with `apikey` + Bearer headers, accepts only when response has `id`. Logic mirrors `AuthGuard.verifySupabaseToken` byte-for-byte (same env-var precedence, same trailing-slash stripping, same fall-back-to-NEXT_PUBLIC_ key); inlining rather than extracting a shared `AuthService.verifyToken` keeps this commit scoped to the gateway — a future consolidation would replace both copies simultaneously. **Master-CEO note:** Supabase tokens don't carry the platform `isMasterCeo` claim (that lives in `PlatformAccessService` and is applied by `AuthGuard` for HTTP requests). WS Supabase users get `isMasterCeo: false`; documented inline so future contributors don't reproduce the cross-tenant bypass by adding the master-CEO claim to a forged Supabase token. **Spec coverage:** 7 new tests (`Supabase token fallback` describe) bringing the gateway spec to 23/23. Coverage: env-vars-missing → reject (fetch not called), valid 200+id → accept (correct URL + headers asserted, trailing-slash stripped from URL), `NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY` fallback when `SUPABASE_ANON_KEY` unset, Supabase 401/non-OK → reject, Supabase 200 but no `id` → reject (anti-shape-confusion), `fetch` throws → reject (network error fail-closed), **legacy JWT wins when valid — Supabase fetch never called** (ordering invariant locked). Spec mocks `global.fetch`, restores in `afterEach`; saves/restores env vars too. **Verification:** `tsc --noEmit` clean across `backend-node`; `npx jest src/ai-advisor/ai-advisor.gateway.spec.ts` → **23/23 green** in 1.0s (was 16, +7 Supabase cases); `claude-peers conflict-check` OK; atomic stage+commit via `git commit -- <pathspec>` per protocol. **Wave fully complete:** every documented IDOR/auth follow-up from `docs/security/IDOR_RESIDUAL_AUDIT.md` is now closed (155 routes + 3 ownership patterns + ai-advisor HTTP + WS + Supabase + CPA defense-in-depth + privacy filter + userId chain). — `backend-node/src/ai-advisor/ai-advisor.gateway.ts`, `backend-node/src/ai-advisor/ai-advisor.gateway.spec.ts`

- 2026-05-16 — **security(cpa): `FirmOwnsClientGuard` — close peer-2's flagged defense-in-depth gap on `cpa-client.controller.ts:removeClient` (replaces `verify:institution-scope-skip` exemption with active class-level guard).** Closes the explicit follow-up peer-2 flagged in `5dbd7880`'s commit body: *"the CPA skip should become a real primitive — a `FirmOwnsClientGuard` that asserts `CpaClientRelationship` exists for the `(firmId, institutionId)` pair — so the CPA route gets defense-in-depth instead of relying on `CpaClientService.removeClient`'s internal check alone."* Pre-fix: `DELETE /api/cpa/firms/:firmId/clients/:institutionId` carried only `AuthGuard + RolesGuard` at the controller layer; the firm-client relationship check happened ONLY inside `CpaClientService.removeClient`. Single point of failure — any future refactor that bypassed that service method (e.g. a new bulk-remove endpoint sharing the controller) would silently lose the check. **New `FirmOwnsClientGuard` mirrors `InstitutionScopeGuard` + `OrgMembershipGuard` contract:** 401 if no user, master-CEO bypass with no DB hit, pass-through when `:firmId` or `:institutionId` is absent (lets the guard sit at class level on the mixed-route controller — `GET /clients`, `GET /dashboard`, `POST /clients/bulk`, `POST /upload-quarterly` have no `:institutionId` and pass through; only `DELETE /clients/:institutionId` actually triggers the lookup), `findFirst` on `cpaClientRelationship` filtered by `(cpaFirmId: firmId, institutionId, removedAt: null)` — note schema-canonical field name `cpaFirmId` per `prisma/schema.prisma:122` (the existing service uses `firmId` which appears to rely on undocumented Prisma behavior; not in scope to fix here, my guard uses the verified-correct field), 404 if no active relationship (treats soft-removed `removedAt != null` as not-existing), 403 fail-closed on Prisma exception. **Wiring:** class-level `@UseGuards(AuthGuard, RolesGuard, FirmOwnsClientGuard)` on `CpaClientController`. `FirmOwnsClientGuard` added to `CpaModule.providers`. The existing `verify:institution-scope-skip` comment stays — InstitutionScopeGuard genuinely doesn't apply here (CPA users aren't workspace owners of their client institutions), the new guard is the parallel CPA-specific primitive that the skip comment originally anticipated as future work. **Spec coverage:** 9 unit tests in `cpa/guards/firm-owns-client.guard.spec.ts` (NEW) — 401 no user, master-CEO bypass, pass-through with no `:institutionId`, pass-through with no `:firmId`, allows on active relationship, 404 on no relationship, 404 on soft-removed (`removedAt != null`) relationship, 403 fail-closed on Prisma throw, userId wider chain. **Verification:** `tsc --noEmit` clean across `backend-node`; **45/45 green** across the 3 cpa specs (was 36, +9 new guard tests); `npm run verify:institution-scope` still reports `60 controllers scanned [institution-scope: 132/132, org-membership: 12/12, close-cycle-membership: 11/11], 0 violations` — refactor preserves the existing CI invariant (the new guard pattern is not yet scanned by the verifier; a follow-up could extend it to a 4th pattern). - 2026-05-16 — **chore(ai-advisor): widen `deleteSession` userId chain to `userId ?? id ?? sub` (small bug fix matching `ask()` + `getSessionHistory()`).** `AuthGuard:271` sets `req.user.userId` as the canonical post-auth field, but the controller's `deleteSession` handler read `req.user?.id ?? req.user?.sub ?? ''` — skipping the canonical field. For JWTs that don't carry an `id` or `sub` claim (or carry them with different shapes), the chain hits `''`, the Prisma `deleteMany` filter becomes `where: { sessionId, userId: '' }`, no rows match even for the legitimate owner, and the service returns 404 — making delete silently broken for all of those callers. Widened to `userId ?? id ?? sub` matching `ask()` (e88ae20c) and `getSessionHistory()` (9dbf57df). Single-line code change + 7-line comment explaining the why; spec strengthened with two new cases asserting `userId`-first read and the legacy-chain fallthrough through `id` then `sub`. **Verification:** `tsc --noEmit` clean; `npx jest src/ai-advisor/ai-advisor.controller.security.spec.ts` → **10/10 green** (was 8, +2 from new fallback tests). `claude-peers conflict-check` OK. — `backend-node/src/ai-advisor/ai-advisor.controller.ts`, `backend-node/src/ai-advisor/ai-advisor.controller.security.spec.ts`

- 2026-05-16 — **IDOR follow-up #5: close intra-institution session privacy leak via `getSessionHistory` userId filter (HTTP + WS + LLM-context paths).** Closes the privacy gap documented in `docs/security/IDOR_RESIDUAL_AUDIT.md` after `b2a64c25`'s WS hardening: even with all institution-ownership checks in place (`InstitutionScopeGuard.verifyOwnership` running on every entry surface), `ConversationHistoryService.getSessionHistory(institutionId, sessionId, limit)` returned messages by (institutionId, sessionId) without filtering by userId. Two users in the same institution sharing a sessionId — intentional (collaborative session) or guessed (UUID enumeration is impractical but not impossible) — could read each other's conversation history. Worse: `AiAdvisorService.ask()`/`streamAsk()` load history *as LLM context*, so the model would see the other user's prior questions and assistant responses and synthesize an answer that leaked them. **Fix:** add optional `userId?: string` 4th param to `getSessionHistory`; conditionally include `userId` in the Prisma `where` clause (`...(userId ? { userId } : {})` — empty-spread keeps the type literal). All 4 callers updated to pass it: `ai-advisor.service.ts:160` (`ask` LLM context), `ai-advisor.service.ts:312` (`streamAsk` LLM context), `ai-advisor.controller.ts:getSessionHistory` (HTTP `GET /sessions/:institutionId/:sessionId`), `ai-advisor.gateway.ts:handleHistory` (WS `history` event). Optional param preserved for forward-compat with future cross-user audit views — explicitly documented in the JSDoc. Controller widens userId chain to `userId ?? id ?? sub` (matches `ask()` from `e88ae20c`). **Spec strengthening:** existing gateway spec for `handleHistory` upgraded from `toHaveBeenCalledTimes(1)` to `toHaveBeenCalledWith('inst-1', 'sess-1', 50, 'user-1')` — locks the userId-forwarding contract at the WS layer with an exact-args assertion. New 2-test suite added to `ai-advisor.controller.security.spec.ts` covering the HTTP `GET /sessions/:institutionId/:sessionId` path: (a) userId forwarded with canonical `req.user.userId`, (b) wider chain falls through to `req.user.sub` for legacy JWT shapes. **Verification:** `tsc --noEmit` clean across `backend-node`; **36/36 green** across the 3 ai-advisor specs (gateway 17 + controller security 9 + service 11 — was 34, +2 from the new HTTP getSessionHistory tests). `claude-peers conflict-check` OK. Atomic stage+commit via `git commit -- <pathspec>` (protocol cardinal rule). — `backend-node/src/ai-advisor/conversation-history.service.ts`, `backend-node/src/ai-advisor/ai-advisor.service.ts`, `backend-node/src/ai-advisor/ai-advisor.controller.ts`, `backend-node/src/ai-advisor/ai-advisor.gateway.ts`, `backend-node/src/ai-advisor/ai-advisor.gateway.spec.ts`, `backend-node/src/ai-advisor/ai-advisor.controller.security.spec.ts`

- 2026-05-16 — **IDOR follow-up #4: close CRITICAL ai-advisor WebSocket auth bypass — JWT handshake verify + `verifyOwnership()` per-handler, same primitive as HTTP path.** Closes the CRITICAL finding flagged in audit decision `84faea03` and documented in `docs/security/IDOR_RESIDUAL_AUDIT.md`. Pre-fix: `AiAdvisorGateway.handleConnection` read `userId` from `client.handshake.auth.userId || client.handshake.query.userId || 'anonymous'` — **zero JWT verification**, just trust whatever string the client sends. Compounded with body-trust on `payload.institutionId` in the `ask` and `history` event handlers, an attacker who knew the WS endpoint URL could (a) connect with `?userId=anyone` query param, (b) emit `ask` events for any institutionId — billing Anthropic API calls on your account on behalf of the impersonated user/institution, (c) emit `history` events to read any session's messages. The HTTP `POST /ask` IDOR was closed by `e88ae20c`+`4f9e2728`'s `verifyOwnership()` call, but the WS `ask` path bypassed the entire HTTP stack and invoked the same `streamAsk` service — so the HTTP fix was a half-fix until this commit. **Three layers shipped in this commit:** (1) **Handshake-time JWT verify.** `handleConnection` extracts a bearer token from `client.handshake.auth.token` (preferred — socket.io's standard auth channel) or the legacy `Authorization: Bearer <token>` header. Verified via the same `JwtService` `AuthGuard` uses (re-exported from `AuthModule`, now imported by `AiAdvisorModule` — clean DI, no JwtModule duplication, no circular dep risk since `AuthModule` is a leaf in the dep graph). The verified `userId` (from `payload.userId` or `payload.sub`) and `isMasterCeo` flag (from `payload.access.isMasterCeo`) land on `client.data.user`. Connections with missing/invalid/payload-shape-bad tokens get an `error` event with `code: 'UNAUTHENTICATED'` and `client.disconnect(true)` — fail-closed, no anonymous fallback. (2) **Per-handler defense-in-depth user check.** `handleAsk` and `handleHistory` re-validate `client.data.user` and emit `code: 'UNAUTHENTICATED'` + return early if absent. A future regression on the connection path can't silently re-open the bypass — the handler still rejects. (3) **`verifyOwnership` before service call.** Same `InstitutionScopeGuard.verifyOwnership(institutionId, userId, isMasterCeo)` primitive as the HTTP controller fix (`e88ae20c`). **Single source of truth for the institution-ownership contract across HTTP + WebSocket.** On rejection, emits `code: 'FORBIDDEN'` with the underlying error message — same WARN logs as URL-path code paths. **Why a guard primitive call rather than copy-pasting the lookup:** the user's directive at the start of this session — *connect all workers to kernel* — is exactly what this single primitive enables. HTTP URL-param routes use `canActivate` via `@UseGuards`; HTTP body-param routes (the `ai-advisor` controller `POST /ask` from `e88ae20c`) inject and call `verifyOwnership`; WebSocket event handlers (this commit) inject and call `verifyOwnership`. Same Prisma lookup, same 403/404 semantics, same WARN denial logs, same fail-closed-on-Prisma-throw, same master-CEO bypass. Three entry surfaces, one authorization kernel. Peer-2's CI verifier (`scripts/verify-institution-scope-guard.mjs` — now ALSO covering `org-membership: 12/12` and `close-cycle-membership: 11/11` from a follow-up landing — total **155 routes provably guarded across 3 patterns**) cannot inspect the WS handlers (it scans `@UseGuards` decorators on controller files), so the gateway-level enforcement is locked by the spec instead. **Spec coverage:** 16 tests in `backend-node/src/ai-advisor/ai-advisor.gateway.spec.ts` (NEW). 6 handshake-verify cases (no token in any source, `JwtService.verify` throws, payload no `userId`/`sub`, valid `auth.token`, valid `Authorization: Bearer` header, master-CEO flag forwarding). 6 `handleAsk` cases (unauthenticated rejection, INPUT_INVALID on bad payload, `verifyOwnership` invocation order BEFORE `streamAsk` via `mock.invocationCallOrder`, FORBIDDEN propagation skips `streamAsk`, master-CEO forwarding, happy-path event sequence). 4 `handleHistory` cases (parallel coverage of unauthenticated, malformed payload, ordering, FORBIDDEN propagation). Direct-construction style mirrors `ai-advisor.controller.security.spec.ts` (`e88ae20c`'s pattern) and `close.controller.spec.ts`. **Module wiring:** `AiAdvisorModule` adds `AuthModule` to imports (re-exports `JwtModule` per `auth.module.ts:43`). No circular dep — `AuthModule` is fundamental, doesn't reference downstream modules. `JwtService` flows to the gateway constructor via standard DI. **Audit-doc updates:** `docs/security/IDOR_RESIDUAL_AUDIT.md` marks WS gateway section as CLOSED with the full layer breakdown (L8 transport / L7 handshake / L6 event / L5 service / L4 service-internal / L3 RLS / L2 logging). Documents the Supabase-JWT follow-up: `JwtService.verify()` only handles legacy JWTs; if WS clients use Supabase tokens in production, mirror `AuthGuard.verifySupabaseToken()` in the gateway's `verifyClientToken()` helper. **Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit -p tsconfig.json` clean across `backend-node`; `npx jest src/ai-advisor/ai-advisor.gateway.spec.ts` → **16/16 green** in 1.0s; `npm run verify:institution-scope` → `60 controller(s) scanned [institution-scope: 132/132, org-membership: 12/12, close-cycle-membership: 11/11], 0 violation(s)` (refactor preserved CI invariant on all three patterns). `claude-peers conflict-check` OK. **Cross-session protocol applied (per `feedback_inter_session_protocol.md`):** scope claimed before write; explicit-pathspec staging via `git commit -- <pathspecs>` (the cardinal rule that prevents the index-race that split `e88ae20c`+`4f9e2728`); decision will be archived after commit; claim released on completion. — `backend-node/src/ai-advisor/ai-advisor.gateway.ts`, `backend-node/src/ai-advisor/ai-advisor.module.ts`, `backend-node/src/ai-advisor/ai-advisor.gateway.spec.ts` (NEW), `docs/security/IDOR_RESIDUAL_AUDIT.md`

- 2026-05-16 — **Tenant-scope verifier generalized to multi-rule: now enforces both `InstitutionScopeGuard` AND `OrgMembershipGuard`. 155 routes provably guarded, 0 violations.** Closes the audit doc's "extend the CI grep to enforce the org-membership pattern" follow-up. The verifier (`backend-node/scripts/verify-institution-scope-guard.mjs`) was rewritten from one hardcoded rule (`:institutionId` → `InstitutionScopeGuard`) into a config-driven framework with a `RULES` array at the top of the file. Three rules currently registered: **`institution-scope`** (`:institutionId` → `InstitutionScopeGuard`, `Workspace.ownerId` model — 132 routes), **`org-membership`** (`:orgId` → `OrgMembershipGuard`, `OrganizationMember` model — 12 routes), **`close-cycle-membership`** (`:cycleId` → `OrgMembershipGuard` 1-hop resolution via `CloseCycle.organizationId` — 11 routes). Each rule carries its own `canonicalParam`, `variants[]` (param-name R1 detector), `guard` class name, `model` label, and `docRef`. R1 (variant param names) and R2 (guard required) iterate the rule set so adding a new tenancy root is one `RULES.push()` + one self-test case — no parser changes. The parser was generalized in lockstep: `classGuards: Set<string>` and `block.guards: Set<string>` replace the prior boolean `hasIsg` flag; identifiers inside `@UseGuards(...)` are extracted via `/\b[A-Z][A-Za-z0-9_]*\b/g` so any guard name registered in a `RULES` entry can be detected. The skip keyword was widened from `// verify:institution-scope-skip` to the generic `// verify:tenant-scope-skip — <reason>` (legacy keyword still accepted for backward compat — locked by a self-test case). **Self-test grew from 11 → 18 cases** covering institution-scope happy paths + base-path inheritance + variant R1, org-membership class-guard + cycle 1-hop + variants, cycle-membership no-guard R2, and 4 skip-mechanism contracts (legacy alias OK, missing-reason fails, one-shot doesn't leak, multi-rule independence so one route can satisfy one rule while violating another). All 18 pass. **Live run surfaced 5 violations in `expenses.controller.ts`** — the audit-doc-flagged case using inline `verifyOrgMembership(orgId, userId)` helper instead of class-level `@UseGuards(OrgMembershipGuard)`. The pattern is intentional: expenses supports `:orgId === 'auto'` / `'default'` escape values that resolve to `OrganizationMember.findFirst({where: {userId}})` — a flow `OrgMembershipGuard.canActivate` would 403 because there's no org with id `'auto'`. Closing properly requires either (a) extending `OrgMembershipGuard` with escape-path awareness or (b) refactoring expenses away from sentinel orgId URL values. Either is a separate wave; for this commit each `:orgId` route in `expenses.controller.ts` carries a `// verify:tenant-scope-skip` comment with the rationale (the first route documents the full pattern, the others reference it). The verifier accepts the skip; missing-reason still fails. **npm scripts**: `verify:tenant-scope` is the new primary name (chained into `npm run lint`); `verify:institution-scope` kept as alias for the prior wave's prose. Both run the same script. **Per-rule summary line on the verifier**: `60 controller(s) scanned [institution-scope: 132/132, org-membership: 12/12, close-cycle-membership: 11/11], 0 violation(s)` — every tenancy root reports its own pass/total so a regression on any one surfaces with the rule id, not buried in a global count. **Memory updated**: `feedback_cerniq_idor_guard.md` now documents the multi-rule pattern + the `RULES.push()` recipe for adding new tenancy roots. **Follow-up unblocked**: a `FirmOwnsClientGuard` for the CPA cross-tenant skip becomes a one-config-entry addition once the guard itself ships. — `backend-node/scripts/verify-institution-scope-guard.mjs`, `backend-node/package.json`, `backend-node/src/expenses/expenses.controller.ts`


- 2026-05-16 — **IDOR follow-up #3: close ai-advisor `POST /ask` body-trust IDOR via `InstitutionScopeGuard.verifyOwnership()` primitive + flag CRITICAL WS-gateway auth bypass.** Closes the first of the two ai-advisor IDORs flagged in `docs/security/IDOR_RESIDUAL_AUDIT.md` (`POST /api/ai-advisor/ask` trusted `body.institutionId` and called `getInstitutionContext(institutionId)` with no ownership check — class-level `InstitutionScopeGuard` passes through because `:institutionId` is not in the URL). The second ai-advisor IDOR (`DELETE /sessions/:sessionId`) was closed earlier in this wave by a peer's userId-scoping of `ConversationHistoryService.deleteSession()` — bundled into this commit because peer's edit was unstaged at audit time and we share a working tree, and because both fixes are co-documented in this commit's audit-doc update. **Approach:** refactor `backend-node/src/agent-api/guards/institution-scope.guard.ts` to expose `verifyOwnership(institutionId, userId, isMasterCeo): Promise<void>` as a public method. `canActivate()` now extracts the args from `req` and delegates — same lookup, same 403/404, same WARN denial logs, same fail-closed-on-Prisma-throw, master-CEO bypass preserved. The guard becomes a multi-context primitive: URL-param routes use `canActivate` (via class-level `@UseGuards`); body-param routes (and future SSE/WebSocket consumers) inject the guard and call `verifyOwnership` directly. `AiAdvisorController.ask()` constructor gains `private readonly institutionScope: InstitutionScopeGuard` (already in `AiAdvisorModule.providers` from peer's prior commit) and calls `await this.institutionScope.verifyOwnership(institutionId, userId, !!req.user?.access?.isMasterCeo)` BEFORE invoking the LLM service. **Why a guard refactor rather than a service-layer check or a parallel `InstitutionAccessService`:** peer-1's `8f69c148` commit body explicitly rolled back an `InstitutionAccessService` primitive on the rationale that *the codebase has chosen the InstitutionScopeGuard model and adding a parallel primitive would create two ways to express the same contract*. Extracting `verifyOwnership` from inside the existing guard preserves that single-source-of-truth contract while adding the missing surface for body-param contexts. Peer-2's CI verifier (`scripts/verify-institution-scope-guard.mjs` from earlier in the wave) is unaffected — it scans `@UseGuards` decorators in controller files, not the guard implementation. **userId chain widening:** `ai-advisor.controller.ts:ask()` previously read `req.user?.id ?? req.user?.sub ?? 'anonymous'`, but `AuthGuard:271` canonically sets `req.user.userId`. The fallback chain skipped the canonical field — `'anonymous'` would have been compared to `Workspace.ownerId` and always failed (or coincidentally matched the JWT `sub` claim if non-OAuth-shape JWTs were in use). Widened to `userId ?? id ?? sub ?? 'anonymous'`. The `deleteSession()` and `listSessions()` paths still use the legacy chain — flagged as a follow-up normalization in the audit doc rather than touched in this commit (peer just shipped the deleteSession edit; touching it again would be a courtesy violation). **Spec hygiene:** 7-test focused security spec at `backend-node/src/ai-advisor/ai-advisor.controller.security.spec.ts` (NEW) — direct-construction style mirroring `close.controller.spec.ts`, asserts (a) `verifyOwnership` runs BEFORE `aiAdvisor.ask()` via `jest.fn().mock.invocationCallOrder` ordering, (b) `Forbidden` propagates without LLM invocation, (c) `NotFound` propagates without LLM invocation, (d) master-CEO flag forwarded, (e) all three userId-shape fallbacks (`userId` / `id` / `sub`) work, (f) deleteSession passes userId so cross-user deletes are filtered, (g) service `NotFound` propagates on (sessionId, userId) miss. Plus 5 new tests on `institution-scope.guard.spec.ts` covering `verifyOwnership` directly: ownership-OK, ownership-fail, master-CEO bypass, NotFound on missing institution, fail-closed on Prisma throw. Existing 8 `canActivate` tests preserved unchanged — refactor is behavior-neutral on the canActivate path. **NEW CRITICAL finding flagged in audit doc:** `ai-advisor.gateway.ts` (Socket.io `@WebSocketGateway({namespace:'ai-advisor'})`) has **zero JWT verification**. `handleConnection` reads `userId` from `client.handshake.auth.userId` OR `client.handshake.query.userId` OR literal `'anonymous'` — no token verification, just trust whatever string the client supplies. Compounded with body-trust on `payload.institutionId` in the `ask` and `history` event handlers, an attacker who knows the WS endpoint URL can: (1) connect with `?userId=anyone` query param, (2) emit `ask` events for any institutionId — billing Anthropic API calls on your account on behalf of the impersonated user/institution, (3) emit `history` events to read any session's messages. The HTTP `POST /ask` IDOR is now closed by this commit's `verifyOwnership` call, but the WS `ask` path bypasses the entire HTTP stack and invokes the same `streamAsk` service. **This jumps the queue ahead of cosmetic CI work** — a fintech security review would lock down on this finding. Audit doc has a fix sketch (handshake-middleware JWT verification + `verifyOwnership` calls in event handlers + focused gateway spec + consider feature-flagging WS until the auth fix lands). **Other follow-ups documented:** (a) `GET /api/ai-advisor/sessions/:institutionId/:sessionId` is institution-scoped (guard catches) but not user-filtered — privacy gap surfaces in multi-member-org futures; tighten by adding `userId` to `getSessionHistory()` mirroring `listSessions(institutionId, userId)`. (b) userId-extraction inconsistency repo-wide — normalize to `userId ?? id ?? sub` everywhere. (c) `AiAdvisorService.getInstitutionContext()` signature drift — `ai-advisor.service.spec.ts` mid-update to a 2-arg `(institutionId, userId)` signature pushing ownership INTO the service (a complementary defense-in-depth approach); spec is currently failing because implementation hasn't caught up. Either revert the spec change (since this commit's controller-layer fix closes the same IDOR) OR update the service. Tracked. **Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit -p tsconfig.json` clean across `backend-node`; `npx jest src/ai-advisor/ai-advisor.controller.security.spec.ts src/agent-api/guards/institution-scope.guard.spec.ts` → **20/20 green** (7 new security + 13 guard, 8 original `canActivate` + 5 new `verifyOwnership`); structured `WARN denied` and `ERROR institution lookup failed` log lines visible in test output (operator-dashboard ready, both URL-path and body-path code paths emit identical signals). `claude-peers conflict-check` → OK against 5 active peer claims. **Coordination note:** committed alongside several peer's in-flight unstaged work (`backend-node/src/ai-advisor/ai-advisor.service.{ts,spec.ts}`, `frontend/e2e/auth.spec.ts`) — explicit `git add` of my 6 paths only, never `-A`. Released narrowed `claude-peers claim` (sid=8f694e66) before staging. — `backend-node/src/agent-api/guards/institution-scope.guard.ts`, `backend-node/src/agent-api/guards/institution-scope.guard.spec.ts`, `backend-node/src/ai-advisor/ai-advisor.controller.ts`, `backend-node/src/ai-advisor/conversation-history.service.ts`, `backend-node/src/ai-advisor/ai-advisor.controller.security.spec.ts` (NEW), `docs/security/IDOR_RESIDUAL_AUDIT.md`

- 2026-05-15 — **`.husky/pre-commit`: add `prettier --check` stage on staged backend-node files (closes 3× flagged follow-up).** The polish wave's recurring failure mode — backend prettier drift reaches CI Backend Tests' eslint stage and fails the run (eslint runs `prettier/prettier` as a rule). Three commits this wave shipped pure prettier fixes — `9d553158` (4 backend files), `6c4bfcfe` (peer-1's `market-data.controller.spec.ts`), plus the same gap flagged a third time in the `de1c90b6` wrap-up — because the husky hook only ran `tsc --noEmit` + secret-scan, never `prettier --check`. This commit closes the gate at write-time so the next prettier drift fails locally in ~2s instead of CI in ~5min. **Implementation:** new stage in `.husky/pre-commit` between the tsc check and the landing-gate. `git diff --cached --name-only --diff-filter=ACM` piped through `grep -E '^backend-node/.*\.(ts|js|mjs|json)$'` produces the staged-backend list; `sed 's|^backend-node/||'` strips the prefix so paths resolve against `backend-node/.prettierrc` (the only prettier config in the repo); `( cd backend-node && ... | xargs npx prettier --check )` runs in a subshell so cwd-change doesn't leak. Non-zero exit prints a red error block with the exact remediation command and exits 1. **Design calls (decided with user):** (1) **Block, no auto-fix** — auto-fixing would silently rewrite the user's staged content; explicit block + remediation message is more honest and matches the existing tsc + secret-scan posture. (2) **Backend-only scope** — frontend has its own hard-blocked tsc lint chain from `d9e0d09c`; backend is the actually-failing path. (3) **No bypass env var** — diverges from the `SKIP_LANDING` / `SKIP_CLAIMS` / `SKIP_SECRET_SCAN` convention by deliberate choice; drift is a 1-command fix and `--no-verify` remains the universal escape hatch if ever genuinely needed. **Verification:** three controlled local tests — (a) hook with only `.husky/pre-commit` staged → exit 0 (no backend files match the grep); (b) hook with a clean `backend-node/_prettier-hook-probe.ts` staged → `Checking formatting... All matched files use Prettier code style!` → exit 0; (c) same probe file with formatting drift (`export const probe=1;` missing spaces around `=`) → `[warn] _prettier-hook-probe.ts` → red error block → exit 1. Probe file cleaned up via `git rm --cached -f` + `rm`; no test artifacts left. **Coordination:** peer claim `cerniq:husky-prettier-check` (sid=e66ae6ee). Cerniq peers currently active in this shared tree are `8f694e66` (ai-advisor IDOR service-level fix on `backend-node/src/agent-api/guards/` + `src/ai-advisor/`) and `836a9934` (frontend auth-session mock on `frontend/e2e/auth.spec.ts`) — both non-overlapping with `.husky/pre-commit`. Explicit-path staging only (`git add .husky/pre-commit docs/SESSION_HANDOFF.md`), never `git add -A`, so the peers' unstaged work stays untouched in the shared tree. — `.husky/pre-commit`

- 2026-05-15 — **Frontend coverage threshold lock — D24 pattern applied to test coverage.** Sixth ratchet of this session, third dimension of the lint-time invariant suite (alongside types via `d9e0d09c` and orphan-tests via `6cf84233`). Measured current frontend coverage floor via `npm run test:coverage` → **statements 60.92% / branches 52.54% / functions 55.45% / lines 62.34%** across 89 test files / 701 tests. Set thresholds in `frontend/vitest.config.ts` at the integer floor below current (statements 60, branches 52, functions 55, lines 62) — `~0.5pp` buffer absorbs normal refactor flux but blocks any meaningful regression. Convention: **ratchet upward when coverage rises, never loosen**. **No new plumbing required** — `test:coverage` is already invoked by `root/package.json`'s `verify:frontend` chain (`lint → test → test:coverage → build`), so every existing CI path that runs `verify:frontend` will now enforce the floor. The vitest config carries the contract; CI is unchanged. **Verification:** sanity-checked the gate by temporarily raising the statements threshold to 99 → `npm run test:coverage` exited `1` with `"ERROR: Coverage for statements (60.92%) does not meet global threshold (99%)"`; restored to 60 → exit `0` clean. So the gate genuinely fires (it's not just config-syntax-OK). **Why thresholds in `vitest.config.ts` rather than a separate `vitest.coverage.config.ts`:** single source of truth + `npm run test:coverage` continues to be the one command. Developers running coverage locally during refactoring will see the failure immediately — that's the desired feedback loop, not a problem. **Why global not per-file thresholds:** per-file (`perFile: true`) is brittle in a codebase where many small util files hit 100% and one large untested file pulls aggregate down; one file's drift would always-fail per-file mode. Global threshold matches the actual quality signal: aggregate floor. Per-glob ratchets (e.g. `lib/alm/*.ts` already at 93%+) are a follow-up optimization for the next ratchet wave. **Pattern composition:** the frontend now has **5 lint-time invariants** — `eslint → verify-alm-registry → verify-no-orphan-tests → tsc → coverage`. Three were added this session (`6cf84233`, `d9e0d09c`, this commit). All measurable, all blocking, all rooted in the "lock the floor once it's real" recipe. — `frontend/vitest.config.ts`

- 2026-05-16 — **IDOR follow-up #2: close `CloseController` cross-tenant gap via new `OrgMembershipGuard` (org + cycle scope).** Picks up the wave that `8f69c148` (peer-1, 5 `:institutionId` controllers) and `b86baed8` (peer-2, `realtime-alm/market-data` 3 routes) opened, this time on the org-scoped Close Cockpit surface where tenancy flows through `OrganizationMember` rather than `Workspace.ownerId`. Read-only audit of every `*.controller.ts` outside peer-1/peer-2's already-closed paths produced this matrix: **9 `:institutionId` controllers** (agent-api ×5, alm-analyst, report-artifact, ai-advisor, ncua) all already class-level `@UseGuards(AuthGuard, InstitutionScopeGuard)` per peer-1's contract — no change needed. **`expenses/expenses.controller.ts`** uses a different but functionally equivalent pattern (`AuthTenantGuard` class-level + per-route `verifyOrgMembership(orgId, userId)` private helper, with CSV upload escape paths `auto`/`default` resolving to caller's own org via `OrganizationMember.findFirst({where:{userId}})`) — no IDOR vector. **`close/close.controller.ts`** was the real gap: only `@UseGuards(AuthGuard)` at class level, every `:orgId` route (5 — cycles list/create + GL inspection) and every `:cycleId` route (13 — get/sign-off/reopen/tasks/recs/JEs/flux/activity/binder) trusted the path parameter. `listCycles(orgId)`, `getCycle(cycleId)`, the audit binder pack, and JE history endpoints all returned month-end financial close data without a membership check. UUID-guessing isn't a security model for production finance software. **`OrgMembershipGuard` (NEW, `backend-node/src/close/guards/`) mirrors the `InstitutionScopeGuard` contract** but with two adaptations for the org-scoped model: (1) ownership lookup goes through `OrganizationMember` (compound unique key `(organizationId, userId)`) instead of `Workspace.ownerId === userId`, matching the precedent already established in `expenses.controller.ts:verifyOrgMembership` and `expenses.service`. (2) `:cycleId` routes get a single 1-hop resolver — `prisma.closeCycle.findUnique({where:{id}, select:{organizationId:true}})` then membership check on the resolved org. Schema-level fact that makes this clean: `CloseCycle.organizationId @db.Uuid` is non-null per `prisma/schema.prisma`, so the resolver always succeeds-or-404s, never partial. **Why a parallel guard rather than generalizing `InstitutionScopeGuard`:** institution ownership = single `Workspace.ownerId`, org ownership = multi-member `OrganizationMember` with role bearing. Sharing one guard would conflate the relationships and make the CI grep peer-4 is wiring (active claim sid=4dac2c80 on `scripts/verify-institution-scope-guard.mjs`) ambiguous about which guard applies where. A parallel `OrgMembershipGuard` keeps the contracts crisp — one guard per relationship shape. **Pass-through-when-absent contract preserved** (mirrors peer-1's relaxation in `8f69c148`): if neither `:orgId` nor `:cycleId` is in the route's URL, guard returns `true` and `AuthGuard` upstream is the baseline auth check. This is what makes the guard safe to apply at controller class level on a mixed-route controller — though `CloseController` happens to be 100% scoped (every route carries one of the two params, no global utility routes), so coverage is total. **Master CEO bypass** mirrors `auth.guard.ts` so platform support and audit users keep cross-tenant access. **Fail-closed on Prisma exceptions** — both the cycle resolver and the membership lookup catch all errors and convert to `403`, never silent allow. Same pattern as `InstitutionScopeGuard:62-72`. **Spec hygiene:** 10 unit tests in `close/guards/org-membership.guard.spec.ts` cover the full state machine — 401 with no user, master-CEO bypass with no DB hit, pass-through with neither param, 200 on valid `:orgId` member, 403 on non-member, `:cycleId` → orgId resolution + membership pass, 404 on missing cycle, 403 on cycle-lookup-throws (fail-closed), 403 on membership-lookup-throws (fail-closed), and legacy `req.user.id` shape compatibility. Mirrors `agent-api/guards/institution-scope.guard.spec.ts`'s structure so reviewers recognize the contract. **Module wiring:** `OrgMembershipGuard` added to `CloseModule.providers` (mirroring `AlmModule:278`'s pattern peer-1 used — `AgentApiModule` is not `@Global` so the guard's home module owns the DI for it). No new imports needed — `PrismaService` is already global. **Audit doc** at `docs/security/IDOR_RESIDUAL_AUDIT.md` (NEW) captures the full 4-peer sweep matrix (16 `:institutionId` + 2 org-scoped controllers), classifies `cpa-client` as different-threat-model deferral (per peer-2's `b86baed8` body), classifies `expenses` as already-correct-by-different-pattern, lists the `ai-advisor` partial gap as the next residual to close (POST `/ask` trusts `body.institutionId`, DELETE `/sessions/:sessionId` has no scoped param — peer-2's unstaged sweep appears to be approaching this), and documents the L7→L1 defense-in-depth stack (controller guard / service filter / Prisma RLS / Postgres RLS / CI grep / structured logging / this audit). **Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit -p tsconfig.json` clean across `backend-node`; `npx jest src/close/` → **7 suites / 76 tests green** (66 existing + 10 new guard); `npx jest src/close/guards/org-membership.guard.spec.ts` → 10/10 green in 0.36s with structured WARN/ERROR log lines visible (denials and fail-closed paths surfacing as observable signals for operator dashboards); `claude-peers conflict-check` → OK against peer-4's active claim, no overlap. **Coordination note:** committed alongside another peer's residual sweep in flight (10+ unstaged files at audit time across `ai-advisor/`, `cpa-client`, `ncua/`, `report-artifact`, `.github/workflows/ci*.yml`, plus `frontend/components/layout/Sidebar.test.tsx`) — explicit `git add` of my 5 paths only, never `-A`, so peer's working tree stays untouched. Released narrowed `claude-peers claim` (sid=8f694e66) before staging. **Aware of the prior wrap-up entry below**: Backend Tests still red on peer-1's `market-data.controller.spec.ts` reflection-test inversion — that's peer-1's spec to fix; my close-cockpit suite is independent and green. — `backend-node/src/close/close.controller.ts`, `backend-node/src/close/close.module.ts`, `backend-node/src/close/guards/org-membership.guard.ts` (NEW), `backend-node/src/close/guards/org-membership.guard.spec.ts` (NEW), `docs/security/IDOR_RESIDUAL_AUDIT.md` (NEW)
- 2026-05-16 — **CI guard against IDOR regressions: `verify-institution-scope-guard.mjs` + 4 more controllers closed.** Closes both `8f69c148`-flagged follow-ups in one commit: (1) param-name normalization sweep + (3) CI grep-check asserting every `:institutionId` route has the guard. New script at `backend-node/scripts/verify-institution-scope-guard.mjs` (NEW, ~310 LOC including 11-case self-test) walks every `*.controller.ts` under `backend-node/src/` and enforces two fail-closed rules: **R1** — any path-param naming an institution must be exactly `:institutionId` (variants `:instId`, `:institution`, `:institution_id`, `:institutionID` are errors since `InstitutionScopeGuard` reads `req.params.institutionId` literally); **R2** — every route whose effective path (`@Controller(base)` + route decorator) contains `:institutionId` must be guarded by `InstitutionScopeGuard` at class OR method level, with a `// verify:institution-scope-skip — <reason>` opt-out for documented cross-tenant cases. Parser is decorator-block-aware: it correctly handles `@UseGuards` BEFORE `@Get` **and** `@UseGuards` AFTER `@Get` (the live codebase uses both; my first parser only handled the former and produced false-positive R2 violations on the second pattern — caught and fixed mid-session). **Live run surfaced 8 unguarded routes across 4 controllers that the manual `8f69c148` audit missed** — they each have `:institutionId` in a non-leading position (`sessions/:institutionId`, `institution/:institutionId`, `sync/:institutionId`) and slipped past my original `grep -E "@(Get\|Post)\(':institutionId"`. **Closures in this commit:** `ai-advisor.controller.ts` (2 routes — `GET sessions/:institutionId` + `GET sessions/:institutionId/:sessionId`) gains class-level `@UseGuards(AuthGuard, InstitutionScopeGuard)`. `alm/reports/report-artifact.controller.ts` (1 route — `GET institution/:institutionId`) gains `@UseGuards(AuthGuard, InstitutionScopeGuard, RolesGuard)` (preserves the existing role gate). `ncua/ncua.controller.ts` (1 `:institutionId` route + 4 utility routes — **the entire controller was unauthenticated**: zero class-level or method-level guards, every `POST /api/ncua/import` open to any caller) gains class-level `@UseGuards(AuthTenantGuard, InstitutionScopeGuard)` — closes both the auth gap and the IDOR gap simultaneously. `cpa/cpa-client.controller.ts:60` (`DELETE clients/:institutionId`) gets a documented opt-out via `// verify:institution-scope-skip — CPA-firm cross-tenant operation` (rationale inline: CPA firms manage client institutions via `CpaClientRelationship`, not workspace ownership; `RolesGuard` + service-internal firm-ownership check gate this route). The skip mechanism requires a reason — a bare `// verify:institution-scope-skip` comment still fails R2, locked by a self-test case. **`realtime-alm/market-data.controller.ts` deliberately NOT touched this commit.** It has a spec/code mismatch from `b86baed8` (spec asserts class-level, code uses method-level) that's actively being triaged by another session (see prior landing entry's "Backend Tests" diagnosis). Peer-2's next-session plan is to flip the spec's expected/received pairings to match peer-1's method-level intent; my verifier accepts both patterns (current method-level guards on the 3 alert routes satisfy R2), so I don't need to take a position on the spec/code debate to ship this commit. **DI plumbing:** `AiAdvisorModule` and `NcuaModule` get `InstitutionScopeGuard` added to providers (mirrors `AlmModule:278`'s pattern peer-1 used in `8f69c148`); `RealtimeAlmModule` already had it from `b86baed8`. **Wiring:** `backend-node/package.json` chains `verify:institution-scope` into `npm run lint` after eslint — same pattern as `frontend/scripts/verify-no-orphan-tests.mjs` (`6cf84233`) and the just-landed Frontend tsc promotion (`d9e0d09c`). Standalone via `npm run verify:institution-scope`. Self-test via `node scripts/verify-institution-scope-guard.mjs --self-test`. **Verification:** `tsc --noEmit` clean across `backend-node`; `npm run verify:institution-scope` → `60 controller(s) scanned, 132 :institutionId route(s) found, 132 guarded, 0 violation(s)`; `--self-test` → 11/11 cases (8 original rule cases + 3 skip-mechanism cases — skip-with-reason exempts, skip-without-reason still fails, skip is one-shot and doesn't leak to next route); `npx jest` on 3 affected spec suites — `report-artifact.controller.spec.ts` 12/12 (added `InstitutionScopeGuard` to `overrideGuard` chain), `ai-advisor.service.spec.ts` 17/17, `ncua-import.service.spec.ts` 14/14. **Total :institutionId surface now provably guarded:** 132 routes across 60 controllers, with 1 documented exemption (CPA cross-tenant). **Closes follow-ups #1 + #3 from `8f69c148`. Follow-up #2** (multi-tenant team-account `InstitutionAccessService` variant) remains deferred until team-accounts product surface ships. **New follow-up flagged:** the CPA skip should become a real primitive — a `FirmOwnsClientGuard` that asserts `CpaClientRelationship` exists for the `(firmId, institutionId)` pair — so the CPA route gets defense-in-depth instead of relying on `CpaClientService.removeClient`'s internal check alone. — `backend-node/scripts/verify-institution-scope-guard.mjs` (NEW), `backend-node/package.json`, `backend-node/src/ai-advisor/ai-advisor.controller.ts`, `backend-node/src/ai-advisor/ai-advisor.module.ts`, `backend-node/src/alm/reports/report-artifact.controller.ts`, `backend-node/src/alm/reports/report-artifact.controller.spec.ts`, `backend-node/src/cpa/cpa-client.controller.ts`, `backend-node/src/ncua/ncua.controller.ts`, `backend-node/src/ncua/ncua.module.ts`

- 2026-05-16 — **test(e2e): `auth.spec.ts:190` post-portal-migration adjustments — closes the third Frontend E2E failure.** The remaining Playwright failure after `4b4e5755`'s text-drift sweep. Two root causes layered: (1) **2026-04-19 portal migration** made `/dashboard` a bridge that calls `router.replace('/portal/submit?createCycle=1')` in a `useEffect` once `isAuthenticated && onboardingComplete` (`frontend/app/dashboard/page.tsx:108-116`); the spec's `await page.waitForURL('**/dashboard', { timeout: 15000 })` resolved on the brief bridge moment where the logout button doesn't exist yet, then ran assertions before the redirect to `/portal` had attached the portal layout. (2) **Button-text reformatting**: portal layout's logout button text is literally `Log out` (with a space, `frontend/app/portal/layout.tsx:314`), not `Logout`. The spec regex `/logout|salir/i` couldn't match `Log out` because `logout` (6 contiguous chars) doesn't appear inside `Log out` (the space breaks the sequence). Both bugs were dormant until `02a34547` let the workflow actually execute the spec. **Fix:** (a) replace `waitForURL('**/dashboard', ...)` with a function-predicate `waitForURL((url) => /\/(dashboard|portal)(\b|\/)/.test(url.pathname), ...)` that resolves on EITHER the bridge or the final destination — covers the redirect race without coupling to either URL specifically; (b) relax both button regexes: `/log\s*out|cerrar sesi[oó]n|salir/i` (matches `Log out` and `Logout` and future Spanish locales) and `/sign in|iniciar sesi[oó]n|iniciar/i` for the negative assertion; (c) extend the logout `toBeVisible()` with a 15s timeout to allow the redirect chain to settle. Email-in-body assertion (`local-demo@cerniq.local`) preserved — `frontend/app/portal/layout.tsx:320` still renders `<p>{user.email}</p>`, so a hydrated user store implies that text appears. **Why I'm willing to ship this without local repro:** the regex relaxation can't make a passing test fail (it strictly broadens the match), the waitForURL predicate covers a superset of the old URL match, and the timeout extension only buys time. Worst-case CI behavior: same failure with more context. **Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit e2e/auth.spec.ts` clean; `npx eslint --quiet e2e/auth.spec.ts` clean; the new regex character classes cross-verified against source via grep (`Log out` in `portal/layout.tsx:314`; no Spanish logout label currently exists, so the regex includes Spanish forms as future-proofing). — `frontend/e2e/auth.spec.ts`
